Mr. Speaker, I rise today in support of Senate amendments to H.R. 4994, the Medicare Improvements for Patients and Providers Act. This Medicare bill provides strong funding for patient care in America and to help seniors who need it. The bill increases Medicare premiums by $500 for a patient with a family of three to help pay for their health care needs. These funds go directly to doctors and nurses.  Additionally, the bill increases rates for older Americans by 10 to 13 percent, which will mean increased premiums for seniors. The current Medicare law is paid for by both raising taxes on those making over $250,000 and providing seniors a tax break. There would be no impoundment authority under this balanced budget amendment. Under Senate Joint Resolution 71 the balanced budget amendment would apply only if and only if Congress, not the President, adopted a concurrent resolution of the Congress to the effect that the Congress has decided that a balanced budget is in the national interest and to which other measures must be adopted to achieve a joint constitutional balanced budget.  This requires the President to submit to Congress his budget proposed for the balance of 1995. The President must submit that budget to the Congress before the end of May in which Congress may amend or modify the level of spending for the Federal Government.  Any changes made in the President's budget would require at least 60 votes in the Senate. Any amendment to the President's budget which reduces spending more than it increases spending would require at least 60 votes in the Senate.

Mr. Speaker, I rise in support of the legislation at hand, which includes the Retirement, Pension and Investment Funds for Employees Act of 2005. This bill would make technical changes to the Employee Retirement Income Security Act of 1974 to make provisions for private pension plans available in most pension plans that are other than defined benefit plans as of the filing date of such plans. It includes an exemption for funds that are otherwise qualified pension plans because they are private pension plans and not employees plan funds, and it increases the pension fund financing requirement from $50 billion to $100 billion, or $8 billion less annually. It gives private pension plans exemption from mandatory monthly premiums in most defined benefit pension plans.  The investment fund provisions allow private pension plans to use the savings from investment funds for investment purposes or to reduce asset management expenses. Mr. President, today I recognize Frankfort, SD. Founded in 1882, the town of Frankfort will celebrate its 100th anniversary this year.  Located in South Dakota's First Congressional District, Frankfort is known for its rural natural beauty and solid agricultural history. In 1882, William Landmeyer purchased the Pierre Lyle farm near Sillum and located it within the present town limits of Frankfort. A few years later, the future citizens of Frankfort were relocated to Iona. In 1883, Charles J. Pitts donated the land for a minor school and then named the town Iona after Patrick Henry's house. In 1909, the name of the town changed to Frankfort to honor two Frankfort students, Charles F. McElhaney and William D. O'Grady, who all graduated from Iona High School
